<p><b>Abraham</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[a]</a></sup> (originally <b>Abram</b>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[b]</a></sup> is the common <a href="/wiki/Hebrews" title="Hebrews">Hebrew</a> patriarch of the <a href="/wiki/Abrahamic_religions" title="Abrahamic religions">Abrahamic religions</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCarter20008_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCarter20008-7">[5]</a></sup> In Judaism, he is the founding father of the <a href="/wiki/Covenant_(biblical)" title="Covenant (biblical)">special relationship</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> and <a href="/wiki/God_in_Judaism" title="God in Judaism">God</a>; in Christianity, he is the spiritual progenitor of all believers, whether Jewish or <a href="/wiki/Gentile" title="Gentile">non-Jewish</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[c]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWright201072_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWright201072-9">[6]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Abraham_in_Islam" title="Abraham in Islam">in Islam</a>, he is a link in the <a href="/wiki/Prophets_and_messengers_in_Islam" title="Prophets and messengers in Islam">chain of Islamic prophets</a> that begins with <a href="/wiki/Adam" title="Adam">Adam</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Adam_in_Islam" title="Adam in Islam">Adam in Islam</a>) and culminates in <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevenson20128_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevenson20128-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>His life, told in the narrative of the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Genesis" title="Book of Genesis">Book of Genesis</a>, revolves around the themes of posterity and land. Abraham is called by God to leave the house of his father <a href="/wiki/Terah" title="Terah">Terah</a> and settle in the land of <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaan</a>, which God now promises to Abraham and his progeny. This promise is subsequently inherited by <a href="/wiki/Isaac" title="Isaac">Isaac</a>, Abraham's son by his wife <a href="/wiki/Sarah" title="Sarah">Sarah</a>, while Isaac's half-brother <a href="/wiki/Ishmael" title="Ishmael">Ishmael</a> is also promised that he will be the founder of a great nation. Abraham purchases a tomb (the <a href="/wiki/Cave_of_the_Patriarchs" title="Cave of the Patriarchs">Cave of the Patriarchs</a>) at <a href="/wiki/Hebron" title="Hebron">Hebron</a> to be Sarah's grave, thus establishing his right to the land; and, in the second generation, his heir Isaac is married to a woman from his own kin, thus ruling the Canaanites out of any inheritance. Abraham later marries <a href="/wiki/Keturah" title="Keturah">Keturah</a> and has six more sons; but, on his death, when he is buried beside Sarah, it is Isaac who receives "all Abraham's goods" while the other sons receive only "gifts".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESka200926–31_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESka200926–31-10">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most historians view the <a href="/wiki/Patriarchal_age" title="Patriarchal age">patriarchal age</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/The_Exodus" title="The Exodus">the Exodus</a> and the period of the <a href="/wiki/Biblical_judges" title="Biblical judges">biblical judges</a>, as a late literary construct that does not relate to any particular historical era;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNutt199941–42_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNutt199941–42-11">[8]</a></sup> and after a century of exhaustive archaeological investigation, no evidence has been found for a historical Abraham.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDever200198_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDever200198-12">[9]</a></sup> It is largely concluded that the <a href="/wiki/Torah" title="Torah">Torah</a> was composed during the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">early Persian period</a> (late-6th century BCE) as a result of tensions between Jewish landowners who had stayed in <a href="/wiki/Yehud_(Persian_province)" title="Yehud (Persian province)">Judah</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_captivity" title="Babylonian captivity">Babylonian captivity</a> and traced their right to the land through their "father Abraham", and the returning exiles who based their counterclaim on <a href="/wiki/Moses" title="Moses">Moses</a> and the Exodus tradition of the <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">Israelites</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESka2006227–228,_260_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESka2006227–228,_260-13">[10]</a></sup>
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Abraham_cycle">The Abraham cycle</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moln%C3%A1r_%C3%81brah%C3%A1m_kik%C3%B6lt%C3%B6z%C3%A9se_1850.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1043" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Moln%C3%A1r_%C3%81brah%C3%A1m_kik%C3%B6lt%C3%B6z%C3%A9se_1850.jpg/220px-Moln%C3%A1r_%C3%81brah%C3%A1m_kik%C3%B6lt%C3%B6z%C3%A9se_1850.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Moln%C3%A1r_%C3%81brah%C3%A1m_kik%C3%B6lt%C3%B6z%C3%A9se_1850.jpg/330px-Moln%C3%A1r_%C3%81brah%C3%A1m_kik%C3%B6lt%C3%B6z%C3%A9se_1850.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Moln%C3%A1r_%C3%81brah%C3%A1m_kik%C3%B6lt%C3%B6z%C3%A9se_1850.jpg/440px-Moln%C3%A1r_%C3%81brah%C3%A1m_kik%C3%B6lt%C3%B6z%C3%A9se_1850.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moln%C3%A1r_%C3%81brah%C3%A1m_kik%C3%B6lt%C3%B6z%C3%A9se_1850.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Abraham's Journey from Ur to Canaan</i>, by <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zsef_Moln%C3%A1r_(painter)" title="József Molnár (painter)">József Molnár</a>, 1850 (<a href="/wiki/Hungarian_National_Gallery" title="Hungarian National Gallery">Hungarian National Gallery</a>, Budapest)</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure_and_narrative_programs">Structure and narrative programs</span></h3>
<p>The Abraham cycle is not structured by a unified plot centred on a conflict and its resolution or a problem and its solution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESka200928_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESka200928-14">[11]</a></sup> The episodes are often only loosely linked, and the sequence is not always logical, but it is unified by the presence of Abraham himself, as either actor or witness, and by the themes of posterity and land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESka200928-29_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESka200928-29-15">[12]</a></sup> These themes form "narrative programs" set out in Genesis 11:27-31 concerning the sterility of Sarah and 12:1-3 in which Abraham is ordered to leave the land of his birth for the land Yahweh will show him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESka200928-29_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESka200928-29-15">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_and_calling">Origins and calling</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Terah" title="Terah">Terah</a>, the ninth in descent from <a href="/wiki/Noah" title="Noah">Noah</a>, was the father of Abram, <a href="/wiki/Nahor,_son_of_Terah" title="Nahor, son of Terah">Nahor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Haran" title="Haran">Haran</a>. Haran was the father of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lot_(Bible)" title="Lot (Bible)">Lot</a>, who was Abram's nephew; the <a href="/wiki/Abraham%27s_family_tree" title="Abraham's family tree">entire family</a> lived in <a href="/wiki/Ur_of_the_Chaldees" title="Ur of the Chaldees">Ur of the Chaldees</a>. Haran died in his native city, Ur of the Chaldees. Abram married <a href="/wiki/Sarah" title="Sarah">Sarah (Sarai)</a>, who was barren. Terah, Abram, Sarai, and Lot departed for <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaan</a>, but settled in a place named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haran_(biblical_place)" title="Haran (biblical place)">Haran</a>, where Terah died at the age of 205.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[13]</a></sup> God had told Abram to leave his country and kindred and go to a land that he would show him, and promised to make of him a great nation, bless him, make his name great, bless them that bless him, and curse them who may curse him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[14]</a></sup> Abram was 75 years old when he left Haran with his wife Sarai, his nephew Lot, and the substance and souls that they had acquired, and traveled to <a href="/wiki/Shechem" title="Shechem">Shechem</a> in Canaan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[15]</a></sup>
Then he pitched his tent in the east of <a href="/wiki/Bethel" title="Bethel">Bethel</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tissot_Abram%27s_Counsel_to_Sarai.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="323" data-file-width="445" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Tissot_Abram%27s_Counsel_to_Sarai.jpg/220px-Tissot_Abram%27s_Counsel_to_Sarai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Tissot_Abram%27s_Counsel_to_Sarai.jpg/330px-Tissot_Abram%27s_Counsel_to_Sarai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Tissot_Abram%27s_Counsel_to_Sarai.jpg/440px-Tissot_Abram%27s_Counsel_to_Sarai.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tissot_Abram%27s_Counsel_to_Sarai.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Abraham's Counsel to Sarai</i>, watercolor by <a href="/wiki/James_Tissot" title="James Tissot">James Tissot</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1900</span> (<a href="/wiki/Jewish_Museum_(Manhattan)" title="Jewish Museum (Manhattan)">Jewish Museum</a>, New York)</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sarai">Sarai</span></h3>
<p>There was a severe famine in the land of Canaan, so that Abram and Lot and their households traveled to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Egypt</a>. On the way Abram told Sarai to say that she was his sister, so that the Egyptians would not kill him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup> When they entered Egypt, the Pharaoh's officials praised Sarai's beauty to <a href="/wiki/Pharaohs_in_the_Bible" title="Pharaohs in the Bible">Pharaoh</a>, and they took her into the palace and gave Abram goods in exchange. God afflicted Pharaoh and his household with plagues, which led Pharaoh to try to find out what was wrong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[17]</a></sup> Upon discovering that Sarai was a married woman, Pharaoh demanded that Abram and Sarai leave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abram_and_Lot_separate">Abram and Lot separate</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Abraham_and_Lot%27s_conflict" title="Abraham and Lot's conflict">Abraham and Lot's conflict</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Abraham_and_Lot_separating_(State_2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3360" data-file-width="4456" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Abraham_and_Lot_separating_%28State_2%29.jpg/220px-Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Abraham_and_Lot_separating_%28State_2%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Abraham_and_Lot_separating_%28State_2%29.jpg/330px-Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Abraham_and_Lot_separating_%28State_2%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Abraham_and_Lot_separating_%28State_2%29.jpg/440px-Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Abraham_and_Lot_separating_%28State_2%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Abraham_and_Lot_separating_(State_2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Abraham and Lot separate. Gen: 13.7 &amp;.<sup>c</sup></i>, <a href="/wiki/Etching" title="Etching">etching</a> by <a href="/wiki/Wenceslaus_Hollar" title="Wenceslaus Hollar">Wenceslaus Hollar</a>, 17th century (<a href="/wiki/Thomas_Fisher_Rare_Book_Library" title="Thomas Fisher Rare Book Library">Thomas Fisher Rare Book Library</a>, Toronto)</div></div></div>
<p>When they  lived for a while in the <a href="/wiki/Negev" title="Negev">Negev</a> after being banished from Egypt  and came back to the <a href="/wiki/Bethel" title="Bethel">Bethel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ai_(Canaan)" title="Ai (Canaan)">Ai</a> area, Abram's and Lot's sizable herds occupied the same pastures. This became a problem for the herdsmen, who were assigned to each family's cattle. The conflicts between herdsmen had become so troublesome that Abram suggested that Lot choose a separate area, either on the left hand or on the right hand, that there be no conflict amongst brethren. Lot decided to go eastward to the plain of <a href="/wiki/Jordan_River" title="Jordan River">Jordan</a>, where the land was well watered everywhere as far as Zoar, and he dwelled in the cities of the plain toward <a href="/wiki/Sodom_and_Gomorrah" title="Sodom and Gomorrah">Sodom</a>. Abram went south to <a href="/wiki/Hebron" title="Hebron">Hebron</a> and settled in the plain of <a href="/wiki/Mamre" title="Mamre">Mamre</a>, where he built another altar to worship <a href="/wiki/God_in_Abrahamic_religions" title="God in Abrahamic religions">God</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chedorlaomer">Chedorlaomer</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Siddim" title="Battle of Siddim">Battle of Siddim</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meeting_of_abraham_and_melchizadek.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="976" data-file-width="766" decoding="async" height="280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Meeting_of_abraham_and_melchizadek.jpg/220px-Meeting_of_abraham_and_melchizadek.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Meeting_of_abraham_and_melchizadek.jpg/330px-Meeting_of_abraham_and_melchizadek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Meeting_of_abraham_and_melchizadek.jpg/440px-Meeting_of_abraham_and_melchizadek.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meeting_of_abraham_and_melchizadek.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Meeting of Abraham and Melchizedek</i>, canvas by <a href="/wiki/Dieric_Bouts" title="Dieric Bouts">Dieric Bouts the Elder</a>, c. 1464–1467</div></div></div>
<p>During the rebellion of the Jordan River cities, <a href="/wiki/Sodom_and_Gomorrah" title="Sodom and Gomorrah">Sodom and Gomorrah</a>, against <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">Elam</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup> Abram's nephew, Lot, was taken prisoner along with his entire household by the invading Elamite forces. The Elamite army came to collect the spoils of war, after having just defeated the king of Sodom's armies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[20]</a></sup> Lot and his family, at the time, were settled on the outskirts of the Kingdom of Sodom which made them a visible target.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>One person who escaped capture came and told Abram what happened. Once Abram received this news, he immediately assembled 318 trained servants. Abram's force headed north in pursuit of the Elamite army, who were already worn down from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Vale_of_Siddim" title="Battle of the Vale of Siddim">Battle of Siddim</a>. When they caught up with them at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dan_(Bible)" title="Dan (Bible)">Dan</a>, Abram devised a battle plan by splitting his group into more than one unit, and launched a night raid. Not only were they able to free the captives, Abram's unit chased and slaughtered the Elamite King <a href="/wiki/Chedorlaomer" title="Chedorlaomer">Chedorlaomer</a> at Hobah, just north of <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a>. They freed Lot, as well as his household and possessions, and recovered all of the goods from Sodom that had been taken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>Upon Abram's return, Sodom's king came out to meet with him in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King%27s_dale" title="King's dale">Valley of Shaveh</a>, the "king's dale". Also, <a href="/wiki/Melchizedek" title="Melchizedek">Melchizedek</a> king of Salem (<a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>), a priest of <a href="/wiki/Elyon" title="Elyon">El Elyon</a>, brought out bread and wine and blessed Abram and God. Abram then gave Melchizedek a <a href="/wiki/Tithe" title="Tithe">tenth</a> of everything. The king of Sodom then offered to let Abram keep all the possessions if he would merely return his people. Abram refused any deal from the king of Sodom, other than the share to which his allies were entitled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_Bibel_in_Bildern_1860_024.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="911" data-file-width="1124" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_Bibel_in_Bildern_1860_024.png/220px-Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_Bibel_in_Bildern_1860_024.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_Bibel_in_Bildern_1860_024.png/330px-Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_Bibel_in_Bildern_1860_024.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_Bibel_in_Bildern_1860_024.png/440px-Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_Bibel_in_Bildern_1860_024.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_Bibel_in_Bildern_1860_024.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The vision of the Lord directing Abraham to count the stars, woodcut by <a href="/wiki/Julius_Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld" title="Julius Schnorr von Carolsfeld">Julius Schnorr von Carolsfeld</a> from a 1860 <i>Bible in Pictures</i> edition</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Covenant_of_the_pieces">Covenant of the pieces</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Covenant_of_the_pieces" title="Covenant of the pieces">Covenant of the pieces</a></div>
<p>The voice of the Lord came to Abram in a vision and repeated the promise of the land and descendants as numerous as the stars. Abram and God made a covenant ceremony, and God told of the future bondage of Israel in Egypt. God described to Abram the land that his offspring would claim: the land of the <a href="/wiki/Kenites" title="Kenites">Kenites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenizzite" title="Kenizzite">Kenizzites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kadmonites" title="Kadmonites">Kadmonites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biblical_Hittites" title="Biblical Hittites">Hittites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perizzites" title="Perizzites">Perizzites</a>, Rephaims, <a href="/wiki/Amorites" title="Amorites">Amorites</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canaanites" title="Canaanites">Canaanites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Girgashites" title="Girgashites">Girgashites</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jebusite" title="Jebusite">Jebusites</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hagar">Hagar</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hagar" title="Hagar">Hagar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hagar_in_Islam" title="Hagar in Islam">Hagar in Islam</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Foster_Bible_Pictures_0032-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2114" data-file-width="1706" decoding="async" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Foster_Bible_Pictures_0032-1.jpg/220px-Foster_Bible_Pictures_0032-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Foster_Bible_Pictures_0032-1.jpg/330px-Foster_Bible_Pictures_0032-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Foster_Bible_Pictures_0032-1.jpg/440px-Foster_Bible_Pictures_0032-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Foster_Bible_Pictures_0032-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Abraham, <a href="/wiki/Sarah" title="Sarah">Sarah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hagar" title="Hagar">Hagar</a></i>, Bible illustration from 1897</div></div></div>
<p>Abram and Sarai tried to make sense of how he would become a progenitor of nations, because after 10 years of living in Canaan, no child had been born. Sarai then offered her Egyptian handmaiden, <a href="/wiki/Hagar" title="Hagar">Hagar</a>, to Abram with the intention that she would bear him a son.
</p><p>After Hagar found she was pregnant, she began to despise her mistress, Sarai. Sarai responded by mistreating Hagar, and Hagar fled into the wilderness. An angel spoke with Hagar at the fountain on the way to <a href="/wiki/Shur_(Bible)" title="Shur (Bible)">Shur</a>. He instructed her to return to Abram's camp and that her son would be "a wild ass of a man; his hand shall be against every man, and every man's hand against him; and he shall dwell in the face of all his brethren." She was told to call her son <a href="/wiki/Ishmael" title="Ishmael">Ishmael</a>. Hagar then called God who spoke to her "<a href="/wiki/El_Roi" title="El Roi">El-roi</a>", ("Thou God seest me:" KJV). From that day onward, the well was called Beer-lahai-roi, ("The well of him that liveth and seeth me." KJV margin). She then did as she was instructed by returning to her mistress in order to have her child. Abram was 86 years of age when Ishmael was born.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sarah">Sarah</span></h3>
<p>Thirteen years later, when Abram was 99 years of age, God declared Abram's new name: "Abraham" – "a father of many nations".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[26]</a></sup> Abraham then received the instructions for the <a href="/wiki/Covenant_of_the_pieces" title="Covenant of the pieces">covenant of the pieces</a>, of which <a href="/wiki/Religious_male_circumcision" title="Religious male circumcision">circumcision</a> was to be the sign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>God declared Sarai's new name: "<a href="/wiki/Sarah" title="Sarah">Sarah</a>", blessed her, and told Abraham, "I will give thee a son also of her".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[28]</a></sup> Abraham laughed, and "said in his heart, 'Shall a <i>child</i> be born unto him that is a hundred years old? and shall Sarah, that is ninety years old, bear [a child]?'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[29]</a></sup> Immediately after Abraham's encounter with God, he had his entire household of men, including himself (age 99) and Ishmael (age 13), circumcised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Three_visitors">Three visitors</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tissot_Abraham_and_the_Three_Angels.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="311" data-file-width="445" decoding="async" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Tissot_Abraham_and_the_Three_Angels.jpg/260px-Tissot_Abraham_and_the_Three_Angels.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Tissot_Abraham_and_the_Three_Angels.jpg/390px-Tissot_Abraham_and_the_Three_Angels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ec/Tissot_Abraham_and_the_Three_Angels.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tissot_Abraham_and_the_Three_Angels.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Abraham and the Three Angels</i>, watercolor by <a href="/wiki/James_Tissot" title="James Tissot">James Tissot</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1896–1902</span></div></div></div>
<p>Not long afterward, during the heat of the day, Abraham had been sitting at the entrance of his tent by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terebinth" title="Terebinth">terebinths</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mamre" title="Mamre">Mamre</a>. He looked up and saw three men in the presence of God. Then he ran and bowed to the ground to welcome them. Abraham then offered to wash their feet and fetch them a morsel of bread, to which they assented. Abraham rushed to Sarah's tent to order <a href="/wiki/Ash_cake" title="Ash cake">ash cakes</a> made from choice flour, then he ordered a servant-boy to prepare a choice calf. When all was prepared, he set curds, milk and the calf before them, waiting on them, under a tree, as they ate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>One of the visitors told Abraham that upon his return next year, Sarah would have a son. While at the tent entrance, Sarah overheard what was said and she laughed to herself about the prospect of having a child at their ages. The visitor inquired of Abraham why Sarah laughed at bearing a child at her age, as nothing is too hard for God. Frightened, Sarah denied laughing.
</p>
<h3><span id="Abraham.27s_plea"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Abraham's_plea">Abraham's plea</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sodom_and_Gomorrah" title="Sodom and Gomorrah">Sodom and Gomorrah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lot_(biblical_person)" title="Lot (biblical person)">Lot (biblical person)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tissot_Abraham_Sees_Sodom_in_Flames.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="422" data-file-width="528" decoding="async" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tissot_Abraham_Sees_Sodom_in_Flames.jpg/260px-Tissot_Abraham_Sees_Sodom_in_Flames.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tissot_Abraham_Sees_Sodom_in_Flames.jpg/390px-Tissot_Abraham_Sees_Sodom_in_Flames.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tissot_Abraham_Sees_Sodom_in_Flames.jpg/520px-Tissot_Abraham_Sees_Sodom_in_Flames.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tissot_Abraham_Sees_Sodom_in_Flames.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Abraham Sees Sodom in Flames</i>, watercolor by <a href="/wiki/James_Tissot" title="James Tissot">James Tissot</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1896–1902</span></div></div></div>
<p>After eating, Abraham and the three visitors got up. They walked over to the peak that overlooked the 'cities of the plain' to discuss the fate of <a href="/wiki/Sodom_and_Gomorrah" title="Sodom and Gomorrah">Sodom and Gomorrah</a> for their detestable sins that were so great, it moved God to action. Because Abraham's nephew was living in Sodom, God revealed plans to confirm and judge these cities. At this point, the two other visitors left for Sodom. Then Abraham turned to God and pleaded decrementally with Him (from fifty persons to less) that "if there were at least ten righteous men found in the city, would not God spare the city?" For the sake of ten righteous people, God declared that he would not destroy the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>When the two visitors arrived in Sodom to conduct their report, they planned on staying in the city square. However, Abraham's nephew, Lot, met with them and strongly insisted that these two "men" stay at his house for the night. A rally of men stood outside of Lot's home and demanded that Lot bring out his guests so that they may "know" (<abbr title="verse">v.</abbr> 5) them. However, Lot objected and offered his virgin daughters who had not "known" (v. 8) man to the rally of men instead. They rejected that notion and sought to break down Lot's door to get to his male guests,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[33]</a></sup> thus confirming the wickedness of the city and portending their imminent destruction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup>
</p><p>Early the next morning, Abraham went to the place where he stood before God. He "looked out toward Sodom and Gomorrah" and saw what became of the cities of the plain, where not even "ten righteous" (v. 18:32) had been found, as "the smoke of the land went up as the smoke of a furnace."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abimelech">Abimelech</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tissot_The_Caravan_of_Abraham.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="1360" decoding="async" height="485" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Tissot_The_Caravan_of_Abraham.jpg/220px-Tissot_The_Caravan_of_Abraham.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Tissot_The_Caravan_of_Abraham.jpg/330px-Tissot_The_Caravan_of_Abraham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Tissot_The_Caravan_of_Abraham.jpg/440px-Tissot_The_Caravan_of_Abraham.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tissot_The_Caravan_of_Abraham.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Caravan of Abraham</i>, watercolor by <a href="/wiki/James_Tissot" title="James Tissot">James Tissot</a>, before 1903 (<a href="/wiki/Jewish_Museum_(Manhattan)" title="Jewish Museum (Manhattan)">Jewish Museum</a>, New York)</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Endogamy" title="Endogamy">Endogamy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wife%E2%80%93sister_narratives_in_the_Book_of_Genesis" title="Wife–sister narratives in the Book of Genesis">Wife–sister narratives in the Book of Genesis</a></div>
<p>Abraham settled between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kadesh_(South_of_Israel)" title="Kadesh (South of Israel)">Kadesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shur_(Bible)" title="Shur (Bible)">Shur</a> in what the Bible anachronistically calls "the land of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philistine" title="Philistine">Philistines</a>". While he was living in <a href="/wiki/Gerar" title="Gerar">Gerar</a>, Abraham openly claimed that Sarah was his sister. Upon discovering this news, King <a href="/wiki/Abimelech" title="Abimelech">Abimelech</a> had her brought to him. God then came to Abimelech in a dream and declared that taking her would result in death because she was a man's wife. Abimelech had not laid hands on her, so he inquired if he would also slay a righteous nation, especially since Abraham had claimed that he and Sarah were siblings. In response, God told Abimelech that he did indeed have a blameless heart and that is why he continued to exist. However, should he not return the wife of Abraham back to him, God would surely destroy Abimelech and his entire household. Abimelech was informed that Abraham was a prophet who would pray for him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>Early next morning, Abimelech informed his servants of his dream and approached Abraham inquiring as to why he had brought such great guilt upon his kingdom. Abraham stated that he thought there was no fear of God in that place, and that they might kill him for his wife. Then Abraham defended what he had said as not being a lie at all: "And yet indeed <i>she is</i> my sister; she <i>is</i> the daughter of my father, but not the daughter of my mother; and she became my wife."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[37]</a></sup> Abimelech returned Sarah to Abraham, and gave him gifts of sheep, oxen, and servants; and invited him to settle wherever he pleased in Abimelech's lands. Further, Abimelech gave Abraham a thousand pieces of silver to serve as Sarah's vindication before all. Abraham then prayed for Abimelech and his household, since God had stricken the women with infertility because of the taking of Sarah.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>After living for some time in the land of the Philistines, Abimelech and <a href="/wiki/Phicol" title="Phicol">Phicol</a>, the chief of his troops, approached Abraham because of a dispute that resulted in a violent confrontation at a well. Abraham then reproached Abimelech due to his Philistine servant's aggressive attacks and the seizing of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abraham%27s_well" title="Abraham's well">Abraham's well</a>. Abimelech claimed ignorance of the incident. Then Abraham offered a pact by providing sheep and oxen to Abimelech. Further, to attest that Abraham was the one who dug the well, he also gave Abimelech seven ewes for proof. Because of this sworn oath, they called the place of this well: <a href="/wiki/Beersheba" title="Beersheba">Beersheba</a>. After Abimelech and Phicol headed back to <a href="/wiki/Philistia" title="Philistia">Philistia</a>, Abraham planted a    <a href="/wiki/List_of_plants_in_the_Bible" title="List of plants in the Bible">tamarisk</a> grove in Beersheba and called upon "the name of the L<span class="smallcaps" style="font-size:83%">ORD</span>, the everlasting God."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Isaac">Isaac</span></h3>
<p>As had been prophesied in Mamre the previous year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup> Sarah became pregnant and bore a son to Abraham, on the first anniversary of the covenant of circumcision. Abraham was "an hundred years old", when his son whom he named <a href="/wiki/Isaac" title="Isaac">Isaac</a> was born; and he circumcised him when he was eight days old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup> For Sarah, the thought of giving birth and nursing a child, at such an old age, also brought her much laughter, as she declared, "God hath made me to laugh, so that all who hear will laugh with me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup> Isaac continued to grow and on the day he was weaned, Abraham held a great feast to honor the occasion. During the celebration, however, Sarah found Ishmael mocking; an observation that would begin to clarify the birthright of Isaac.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adriaen_van_der_Werff_-_The_Expulsion_of_Hagar_and_Ishmael_-_59.063_-_Rhode_Island_School_of_Design_Museum.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="821" decoding="async" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Adriaen_van_der_Werff_-_The_Expulsion_of_Hagar_and_Ishmael_-_59.063_-_Rhode_Island_School_of_Design_Museum.jpg/220px-Adriaen_van_der_Werff_-_The_Expulsion_of_Hagar_and_Ishmael_-_59.063_-_Rhode_Island_School_of_Design_Museum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Adriaen_van_der_Werff_-_The_Expulsion_of_Hagar_and_Ishmael_-_59.063_-_Rhode_Island_School_of_Design_Museum.jpg/330px-Adriaen_van_der_Werff_-_The_Expulsion_of_Hagar_and_Ishmael_-_59.063_-_Rhode_Island_School_of_Design_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Adriaen_van_der_Werff_-_The_Expulsion_of_Hagar_and_Ishmael_-_59.063_-_Rhode_Island_School_of_Design_Museum.jpg/440px-Adriaen_van_der_Werff_-_The_Expulsion_of_Hagar_and_Ishmael_-_59.063_-_Rhode_Island_School_of_Design_Museum.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Adriaen_van_der_Werff_-_The_Expulsion_of_Hagar_and_Ishmael_-_59.063_-_Rhode_Island_School_of_Design_Museum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Expulsion of Hagar and Ishmael</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Adriaen_van_der_Werff" title="Adriaen van der Werff">Adriaen van der Werff</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1699</span> (<a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_School_of_Design_Museum" title="Rhode Island School of Design Museum">Rhode Island School of Design Museum</a>, Rhode Island)</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ishmael">Ishmael</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ishmael_in_Islam#The_sacrifice" title="Ishmael in Islam">Ishmael in Islam § The sacrifice</a></div>
<p>Ishmael was fourteen years old when Abraham's son Isaac was born to Sarah. When she found Ishmael teasing Isaac, Sarah told Abraham to send both Ishmael and Hagar away. She declared that Ishmael would not share in Isaac's inheritance. Abraham was greatly distressed by his wife's words and sought the advice of his God. God told Abraham not to be distressed but to do as his wife commanded. God reassured Abraham that "in Isaac shall seed be called to thee."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[44]</a></sup> He also said that Ishmael would make a nation, "because he is thy seed".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>Early the next morning, Abraham brought Hagar and Ishmael out together. He gave her bread and water and sent them away. The two wandered in the wilderness of Beersheba until her bottle of water was completely consumed. In a moment of despair, she burst into tears. After God heard the boy's voice, an <a href="/wiki/Angel_of_the_Lord" title="Angel of the Lord">angel of the Lord</a> confirmed to Hagar that he would become a great nation, and will be "living on his sword". A well of water then appeared so that it saved their lives. As the boy grew, he became a skilled <a href="/wiki/Archery" title="Archery">archer</a> living in the wilderness of <a href="/wiki/Desert_of_Paran" title="Desert of Paran">Paran</a>. Eventually his mother found a wife for Ishmael from her home country, the land of Egypt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[46]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Binding_of_Isaac">Binding of Isaac</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_035.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1824" data-file-width="1256" decoding="async" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_035.jpg/220px-Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_035.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_035.jpg/330px-Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_035.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_035.jpg/440px-Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_035.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_035.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Angel Hinders the Offering of Isaac</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>, 1635 (<a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">Hermitage Museum</a>, Saint Petersburg)</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Binding_of_Isaac" title="Binding of Isaac">Binding of Isaac</a></div>
<p>At some point in Isaac's youth, Abraham was commanded by God to offer his son up as a sacrifice in the land of <a href="/wiki/Moriah" title="Moriah">Moriah</a>. The patriarch traveled three days until he came to the mount that God told him of. He then commanded the servants to remain while he and Isaac proceeded alone into the mount. Isaac carried the wood upon which he would be sacrificed. Along the way, Isaac asked his father where the animal for the burnt offering was, to which Abraham replied "God will provide himself a lamb for a burnt offering". Just as Abraham was about to sacrifice his son, he was interrupted by the angel of the Lord, and he saw behind him a "ram caught in a thicket by his horns", which he sacrificed instead of his son. The place was later named as <a href="/wiki/Jehovah-jireh" title="Jehovah-jireh">Jehovah-jireh</a>.  For his obedience he received another promise of numerous descendants and abundant prosperity. After this event, Abraham went to Beersheba.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_years">Later years</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Abraham%27s_family_tree" title="Abraham's family tree">Abraham's family tree</a></div>
<p>Sarah died, and Abraham buried her in the <a href="/wiki/Cave_of_the_Patriarchs" title="Cave of the Patriarchs">Cave of the Patriarchs</a> (the "cave of Machpelah"), near Hebron which he had purchased along with the adjoining field from Ephron the <a href="/wiki/Biblical_Hittites" title="Biblical Hittites">Hittite</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup> After the death of Sarah, Abraham took another wife, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concubine" title="Concubine">concubine</a> named <a href="/wiki/Keturah" title="Keturah">Keturah</a>, by whom he had six sons: <a href="/wiki/Zimran" title="Zimran">Zimran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jokshan" title="Jokshan">Jokshan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medan_(son_of_Abraham)" title="Medan (son of Abraham)">Medan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Midian_(son_of_Abraham)" title="Midian (son of Abraham)">Midian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ishbak" title="Ishbak">Ishbak</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shuah" title="Shuah">Shuah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup> According to the Bible, reflecting the change of his name to "Abraham" meaning "a father of many nations", Abraham is considered to be the progenitor of many nations mentioned in the Bible, among others the <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">Israelites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ishmaelites" title="Ishmaelites">Ishmaelites</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edom" title="Edom">Edomites</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amalek#Amalekites_in_the_Hebrew_Bible" title="Amalek">Amalekites</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kenizzite" title="Kenizzite">Kenizzites</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Midian" title="Midian">Midianites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup> and through his nephew Lot he was also related to the <a href="/wiki/Moab" title="Moab">Moabites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ammon" title="Ammon">Ammonites</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup> Abraham lived to see his son marry <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rebekah" title="Rebekah">Rebekah</a>, and to see the birth of his twin grandsons <a href="/wiki/Jacob_and_Esau" title="Jacob and Esau">Jacob and Esau</a>. He died at age 175, and was buried in the cave of Machpelah by his sons Isaac and Ishmael.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historicity_and_origins_of_the_narrative">Historicity and origins of the narrative</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historicity">Historicity</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_11347_Abrams_well.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="294" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/PikiWiki_Israel_11347_Abrams_well.jpg/260px-PikiWiki_Israel_11347_Abrams_well.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/PikiWiki_Israel_11347_Abrams_well.jpg/390px-PikiWiki_Israel_11347_Abrams_well.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d1/PikiWiki_Israel_11347_Abrams_well.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_11347_Abrams_well.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abraham%27s_well" title="Abraham's well">Abraham's well</a> at <a href="/wiki/Beersheba" title="Beersheba">Beersheba</a>, Israel</div></div></div>
<p>In the early and middle 20th century, leading archaeologists such as <a href="/wiki/William_F._Albright" title="William F. Albright">William F. Albright</a> and <a href="/wiki/G._Ernest_Wright" title="G. Ernest Wright">G. Ernest Wright</a> and biblical scholars such as <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_Alt" title="Albrecht Alt">Albrecht Alt</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Bright_(biblical_scholar)" title="John Bright (biblical scholar)">John Bright</a> believed that the patriarchs and matriarchs were either real individuals or believable composites of people who lived in the "<a href="/wiki/Patriarchal_age" title="Patriarchal age">patriarchal age</a>", the 2nd millennium BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[57]</a></sup> But, in the 1970s, new arguments concerning Israel's past and the biblical texts challenged these views; these arguments can be found in <a href="/wiki/Thomas_L._Thompson" title="Thomas L. Thompson">Thomas L. Thompson</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Historicity_of_the_Patriarchal_Narratives" title="The Historicity of the Patriarchal Narratives">The Historicity of the Patriarchal Narratives</a></i> (1974),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/John_Van_Seters" title="John Van Seters">John Van Seters</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Abraham_in_History_and_Tradition" title="Abraham in History and Tradition">Abraham in History and Tradition</a></i> (1975).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup> Thompson, a literary scholar, based his argument on archaeology and ancient texts. His thesis centered on the lack of compelling evidence that the patriarchs lived in the 2nd millennium BCE, and noted how certain biblical texts reflected first millennium conditions and concerns. Van Seters examined the patriarchal stories and argued that their names, social milieu, and messages strongly suggested that they were <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> creations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreKelle201118–19_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreKelle201118–19-63">[60]</a></sup> Van Seter and Thompson's works were a <a href="/wiki/Paradigm_shift" title="Paradigm shift">paradigm shift</a> in biblical scholarship and archaeology, which gradually led scholars to no longer consider the patriarchal narratives as historical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[61]</a></sup> Some conservative scholars attempted to defend the Patriarchal narratives in the following years, but this has not found acceptance among scholars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[63]</a></sup> By the beginning of the 21st century, archaeologists had given up hope of recovering any context that would make Abraham, Isaac or Jacob credible historical figures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDever200198_and_fn.2_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDever200198_and_fn.2-67">[64]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_of_the_narrative"><span class="anchor" id="Renaming"></span> Origins of the narrative</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abraham%27s_Gate.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Abraham%27s_Gate.jpg/220px-Abraham%27s_Gate.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Abraham%27s_Gate.jpg/330px-Abraham%27s_Gate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Abraham%27s_Gate.jpg/440px-Abraham%27s_Gate.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abraham%27s_Gate.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abraham%27s_Gate" title="Abraham's Gate">Abraham's Gate, Tel Dan, Israel</a></div></div></div>
<p>Abraham's story, like those of the other patriarchs, most likely had a substantial oral prehistory<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPitard200127_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPitard200127-68">[65]</a></sup> (he is mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Ezekiel" title="Book of Ezekiel">Book of Ezekiel</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[66]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Isaiah" title="Book of Isaiah">Book of Isaiah</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup>) and his name is apparently very ancient, as the tradition found in the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Genesis" title="Book of Genesis">Book of Genesis</a> no longer understands its original meaning (probably "Father is exalted" – the meaning offered in Genesis 17:5, "Father of a multitude", is a <a href="/wiki/False_etymology" title="False etymology">popular etymology</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson200223–24_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson200223–24-71">[68]</a></sup> At some stage the <a href="/wiki/Oral_tradition" title="Oral tradition">oral traditions</a> became part of the written tradition of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentateuch" title="Pentateuch">Pentateuch</a>; a majority of scholars believe this stage belongs to the Persian period, roughly 520–320 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESka2009260_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESka2009260-72">[69]</a></sup> The mechanisms by which this came about remain unknown,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnns201226_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnns201226-73">[70]</a></sup> but there are currently two important hypotheses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESka2006217,_227–28_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESka2006217,_227–28-74">[71]</a></sup> The first, called Persian Imperial authorisation, is that the post-Exilic community devised the Torah as a legal basis on which to function within the Persian Imperial system; the second is that the Pentateuch was written to provide the criteria for determining who would belong to the post-Exilic Jewish community and to establish the power structures and relative positions of its various groups, notably the priesthood and the lay "elders".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESka2006217,_227–28_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESka2006217,_227–28-74">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>The completion of the Torah and its elevation to the centre of post-Exilic Judaism was as much or more about combining older texts as writing new ones – the final Pentateuch was based on existing traditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarrConway2010193_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarrConway2010193-75">[72]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Ezekiel" title="Book of Ezekiel">Book of Ezekiel</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[73]</a></sup> written during the Exile (i.e., in the first half of the 6th century BCE), <a href="/wiki/Ezekiel" title="Ezekiel">Ezekiel</a>, an exile in Babylon, tells how those who remained in Judah are claiming ownership of the land based on inheritance from Abraham; but the prophet tells them they have no claim because they do not observe Torah.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESka200943_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESka200943-77">[74]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Isaiah" title="Book of Isaiah">Book of Isaiah</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup> similarly testifies of tension between the people of Judah and the returning post-Exilic Jews (the "<a href="/wiki/Golah" title="Golah">gôlâ</a>"), stating that God is the father of Israel and that Israel's history begins with the Exodus and not with Abraham.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESka200944_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESka200944-79">[76]</a></sup> The conclusion to be inferred from this and similar evidence (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Ezra%E2%80%93Nehemiah" title="Ezra–Nehemiah">Ezra–Nehemiah</a>), is that the figure of Abraham must have been preeminent among the great landowners of Judah at the time of the Exile and after, serving to support their claims to the land in opposition to those of the returning exiles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESka200944_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESka200944-79">[76]</a></sup>
</p>
